### Post by Lyfang on 2012-11-19
Hi, I would like to fix all current problem on a fresh installation of Kubuntu 12.04.1 LTS (Precise Pangolin). These problems and questions include:

*Fan speed that is very high, a noisy loud fan. Windows fan speed is low and regulated.
*High CPU temp. in Kubuntu, much higher than in Windows. sensors shows: CPU Temperature:        +45.0°C  (high = +40.0°C, crit = +90.0°C) 
*Jockey (jockey-kde) suggests installing the ATI/AMD proprietary FGLRX graphics driver or is the driver from AMD's website better? How do I find out what (open source) driver the system is currently using?
*How can I use the ATI temperature sensor with the open source driver? Is there a good open source graphics card temperature monitor?
*I'm searching for a CPU frequency scaling monitor/applet for KDE.
*How do I find out if AMD Cool'n'Quiet is activated?
*How do I switch between Conservative, Ondemand, Performance and Powersave? (CPU profiles)
*Are there AMD optimized kernel builds?
*UFW firewall is inactive by default. See also: [Shieldsup says "failed" when scanning]("https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+bug/185793"). What shall I do? Install Gufw?
*I switched to WebKit in the Konqueror Browser. Is there anything else I might want to do? I have also installed Google Chrome.
*Kopete is installed by default by. I have mostly used Pidgin before. Does Facebook XMPP chat work with Kopete?
*How do I read .nef (raw image format) files on Kubuntu? Is there a good importer for GIMP? How do I convert raw image files in ImageMagick? 
*Okular is installed, but can I fill in forms and save? Should I install Adobe Reader to be able to fill in forms?
*How do I track Internet traffic? How do I reduce traffic usage? Opera Turbo uses compression. I would like to prevent the images from loading, then be able to load them when I want to.
*I need Java. But what Java is best to install? Oracle Java is said to be better for the end user than OpenJDK? Is this true? I was thinking of installing Oracle Java 7 from:

```
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:webupd8team/java
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install oracle-java7-installer
```

*What is the best way to install Windows fonts in Kubuntu?
*Should I use the ODF Text Document as the default format when most people use Microsoft Office with the .docx or .doc format?
*How can I create databases?
*Maintenance for Kubuntu. Is it recommended to use BleachBit to free disk space regularly?
*Best backup software on Kubuntu?
*Automation software to run automated tasks?
*Sofware to help with CMS such as WordPress, Joomla or Drupal?
*I did run sudo dpkg-reconfigure popularity-contest and <Yes>, is this a good idea?

Best Regards,
Lyfang

---

### Post by Lyfang on 2012-11-20
The temperature readings in Windows shows that the CPU temperature is lower. Right now the 'High' is 38°C (100.4°F). Does the Linux kernel have HLT (halt) instruction? Is it recommended to use pwmconfig and fancontrol to regulate and control fan speed? I also have looked after the AMD Radeon HD 6970 proprietary driver on AMD website, but I only find "AMD Catalyst™ 12.10 Proprietary Linux x86 Display Driver". Will this driver work in 12.04.1 LTS when the driver's revision number is 12.10? Any help is greatly appreciated!

### Post by drmrgd on 2012-11-20
Wow!  Lots of questions.  I don't know much about the AMD / ATI drivers, so I'll leave all of that alone.  

I also don't know much about the CPU fan stuff and / or how it's regulated by AMD boards.  I will say that on my Intel board, my CPU is generally running around 35 - 38C.  So, I'm sort of wondering if you have something that's utilizing a lot of CPU cycles and therefore ramping up the CPU temp and causing the fan to run at higher speed to compensate.  Does top show anything constantly running at high CPU usage?

I can knock off a few of the other questions, though, I think:

> *UFW firewall is inactive by default. See also: Shieldsup says "failed" when scanning. What shall I do? Install Gufw?

You can turn on UFW if you like (either commandline or graphical is fine).  It's already installed, and fairly straightforward and easy to set up and run.  Just follow this guide:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UFW](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UFW)
Essentially, just activate UFW, decide what ports to open (if any) and other rules to set, and set your logging preferences.  

> *I need Java. But what Java is best to install? Oracle Java is said to be better for the end user than OpenJDK? Is this true? I was thinking of installing Oracle Java 7 from...

That's generally a good method for installing Java.  That's the way that I currently do it, and it has the benefit of being updated whenever you run your normal updates, as opposed to manually installing it.  When you manually install, you'll have to take care of updating yourself (again manually), and given Java is updated very often to fix security holes and exploits, you'll want to make sure you keep that secure.  Others have also stated that it's a good idea to configure App Armor profiles (something I know very little about at the moment) in addition to keep things even more secure.

> *What is the best way to install Windows fonts in Kubuntu?

Install Ubuntu Restricted Extras:

```
sudo apt-get install ubuntu-restricted-extras
```

That will give you some codecs and Windows fonts.  As a word of caution, in case it comes up, when you're installing you'll be presented with a EULA screen that's not obvious to get around.  Just hit the <Tab> keep to move the cursor to the "OK" button (or is it "yes"...I forget), and hit 'enter' to accept.

The rest of your questions are rather vague ("how can I create databases?"...that's a whole semester course!), and probably more explanation is needed.  In general, when it comes to maintenance,  you can certainly use tools like Bleachbit to clean up the system (many very highly regard this software).  Depending on what you want to backup, there are a myriad of utilities available as well (Rsnapshot, a custom script with Rsync, Deja Dup, Clonezilla, etc.), and it all depends on exactly what you want to backup, what your resources are (i.e. where to put backups and such), and what your comfort level is;  if you don't know shell scripting and /or don't like to work in the terminal, writing a shell script to run a backup job with Rsnapshot or Rsync is not advised.  

OK, that's enough for now.  This list will take some time to chew all the way through!

---

### Post by ankspo71 on 2012-12-03
> *UFW firewall is inactive by default. See also: Shieldsup says "failed" when scanning. What shall I do? Install Gufw?

When you enable ufw (or gufw) you will also want to stop ufw from sending echo replies to incoming echo requests, if you want to get a perfect stealth rating at shields up. 
[http://jamesb.netne.net/blog/shieldsup-and-ufw/](http://jamesb.netne.net/blog/shieldsup-and-ufw/)


> *Maintenance for Kubuntu. Is it recommended to use BleachBit to free disk space regularly?

I use bleachbit in Kubuntu on a near daily basis, but I don't delete anything in the KDE section, like "KDE cache" and "KDE temporary files", because doing so crashes my desktop. Otherwise it is a nice system cleaner.

> *Best backup software on Kubuntu?
I'm not sure what most would call the best, but I like using Grsync because of the numerous options it gives me.

Hope this helps.

---
